Optimization objective mode: risk-adjusted

Versioned optimizer instructions:
Instruction version: spx-0dte-data-aware-v2
Purpose:
Optimize the SPX 0DTE trend scalper without continuing the prior over-filtering path. Do not optimize by deleting trades. Optimize profile-specific confirmation, exits, risk, and missing-0DTE fallback behavior. Do not optimize option/strike-map replay file age thresholds.

Baseline:
Use run_001 as the baseline anchor. Compare every candidate against run_001, the current best isolated candidate, the current best combined candidate, and the latest run. Do not use the last sequential run as the anchor if it was created by cumulative veto tightening.

Core rule:
Do not continue global tightening of entry vetoes. Avoid broad/global filters that improve MAE only by killing profitable trades.

Hard constraints:
- Do not optimize option-dependent profiles for missing/stale/thin 0DTE states. Use only routed fallback profiles for those states.
- Do not globally tighten extended-vwap-rejection-signature.
- Do not globally tighten entry-veto-min-points unless explicitly running a dedicated veto experiment.
- Do not optimize more than one logical family per run.
- Limit each run to 3-5 parameter changes.
- Reject any run that improves MAE only by deleting too many trades.
- Reject any run where trade count drops more than 10% unless net profit and objective improve materially.
- Reject any run where net profit falls more than 2% versus baseline.
- Reject any run where growth quality falls more than 2% versus baseline.
- Reject any run where pnl_per_exposure_hour falls versus baseline.
- Reject candidates that depend on stale 0DTE data older than the configured missing-data policy allows.
- Do not allow option-confirmed profiles to trade when 0DTE data is missing, stale, or thin unless a specific fallback policy allows it.

Primary objective:
Maximize risk-adjusted objective while preserving net profit, growth quality, trade count, exposure efficiency, pnl per exposure hour, profile-level expectancy, and worst MAE control.

Data-state requirement:
Classify trades and candidate behavior as VALID_0DTE, STALE_0DTE, MISSING_0DTE, THIN_0DTE, VALID_1DTE_ONLY, or EXPIRED_0DTE when the analyzer provides the required columns. If those columns are absent, state that limitation and do not invent unsupported config keys.

Missing 0DTE adaptation:
The original master instruction included desired missing-0DTE keys such as missing-0dte-policy.mode, stale-grace-seconds, max-stale-allowed-seconds, fallback-quantity-multiplier, and early-strike-acceptance-seconds. Those keys are not currently in PARAMETER_SPACE, so do not recommend them. Use only router-listed profile keys shown in the filtered instruction_schema and allowed key list.

Run order:
1. Batch G: Missing 0DTE policy using currently available tunables.
2. Batch A: call_wall_acceptance_long.
3. Batch B: squeeze_long take-profit.
4. Batch C: pullback_long distance.
5. Batch D: charm_wall_breakaway_long.
7. Batch F: risk validation.

Promotion rule:

Required result labels:
promote, reject_overfiltered, reject_profit_suppression, reject_trade_starvation, reject_mae_only, reject_stale_data, reject_missing_0dte_loss, flat, needs_profile_breakdown.

Optimization family rule:
Choose exactly one family from instruction_schema.families and only change keys from that family's allowed_keys. Use grid values from that family when possible. If you intentionally leave the grid, explain why and stay within PARAMETER_SPACE.

Profile-specific module overrides use the key format profile.<profile-name>.<setting>, for example profile.breakout_long.es-vwap.slope-min or profile.squeeze_long.order-book.long-min-ofi-1s-normalized.
All profile module settings write to nested module config. Examples: profile.breakout_long.option-strike-map.max-expected-move-position writes to spx500-trend-scalper.strategies.profiles.breakout_long.module-config.option-strike-map.max-expected-move-position; profile.breakout_long.rsi-momentum.threshold writes to module-config.rsi-momentum.threshold; profile.breakout_long.take-profit.distance writes to module-config.take-profit.distance. Do not write flat keys directly inside module-config.
Prefer profile-specific keys when the evidence belongs to one market regime/profile; use global keys only when the change should affect every profile.

Delta/charm strategy profiles are also tunable:
- profile.charm_pin_pullback_long.enabled, profile.charm_pin_pullback_long.long-regime-filter.min-abs-net-charm-next-30m, profile.charm_pin_pullback_long.long-regime-filter.require-pullback-or-lower-fade, profile.charm_pin_pullback_long.take-profit.max-distance
- profile.charm_wall_breakaway_long.enabled, profile.charm_wall_breakaway_long.long-regime-filter.min-distance-above-charm-wall, profile.charm_wall_breakaway_long.long-regime-filter.max-distance-above-charm-wall, profile.charm_wall_breakaway_long.long-regime-filter.min-abs-net-charm-next-30m, profile.charm_wall_breakaway_long.long-regime-filter.require-breakout, profile.charm_wall_breakaway_long.long-regime-filter.require-negative-gamma, profile.charm_wall_breakaway_long.take-profit.multiplier
Use these only when option-strike metrics show that delta/charm regimes separate good trades from bad MAE, slow trades, or missed upside. Dealer charm is estimated only when trade-sign data exists; do not require it unless the metrics actually contain it.

Optimization philosophy:
- Do not add realized stop losses.
- Prefer avoiding bad entries over exiting losers.
- Optimize for the selected objective mode: risk-adjusted.
- Every mode rewards net profit and Sharpe, then penalizes drawdown, MAE, exposure, slow trades, and realized losses with mode-specific weights. Do not use PSR for ranking until the analyzer can distinguish a real zero from a missing/not-calculated PSR.
- In profit-slow-dd mode, increase net profit while explicitly reducing slow >=12h trades and portfolio drawdown; do not sacrifice too much profit for tiny drawdown gains.
- In risk-adjusted mode, keep strong net profit and Sharpe while reducing portfolio drawdown, exposure hours, slow >=12h trades, MAE, and realized losses.
- In drawdown-aware mode, accept lower net profit when the reduction in portfolio drawdown and long underwater exposure is material.
- In growth-quality mode, maximize fast compounding quality: high net profit, many trades, high PnL/exposure hour, high PnL/calendar day, low drawdown, few slow trades, and low MAE. Do not maximize trade count if it simply creates more low-quality exposure.
- Actively test feature switches on/off when historical run context suggests that a switch clusters with better objective score or lower drawdown.
- SPX500 is allowed to sit underwater for long periods when the entry quality is still structurally bullish.
- Treat MAE, exposure hours, and >=12h trades as diagnostic costs, not hard failure conditions.
- Do not chase raw PnL if it creates realized losses, materially worse drawdown, or materially worse entry quality.
- Use ES structure buckets when present to tune score, pullback, higher-low, and higher-high settings from evidence.
- Use the experiment memory to avoid repeating config directions that already hurt net profit, unless you explicitly explain the new combined reason.
- Use the historical run context to identify settings and feature switches that cluster in top net-profit runs versus recent weaker runs.
- Use feature switch guidance before toggling any boolean switch; distinguish gating, scoring, dynamic target, calendar, volatility, order-flow, and trade-maintenance switches by their intended evidence.
- Use analyzer threshold candidates as evidence, not commands. They are one-variable hypothetical filters mined from the latest trades; prefer translating them into existing config keys only when the mapping is structurally valid.
- Use latest bad-MAE entry fingerprints as concrete trade evidence. If a deep-MAE entry escaped an enabled veto, inspect which threshold failed and tune that threshold before inventing a broader gate.
- When signature_hints are present, do not ignore the veto path. Either recommend a surgical veto threshold/switch change, or explicitly explain in the rationale why veto tuning should be skipped because prior experiments hurt score, profit, MAE, exposure, or trade count.
- Treat veto fingerprints as entry diagnostics, not only blockers. Before recommending a veto-only threshold change, inspect entry_improvement_hints and consider whether an upstream entry rule can express the same condition cleanly.
- Use good_trade_fingerprints as protected edge patterns. Do not recommend an entry filter that blocks protected fast/low-MAE/high-PnL/extended-VWAP winners unless the bad-MAE improvement is materially stronger.
- Use bad_vs_good_feature_contrast and counterfactual_if_used_as_entry_filter to avoid broad entry changes that remove too much PnL or fail to improve kept_worst_mae.
- Prefer upstream entry improvements when they preserve the same structural edge and do not broadly starve profitable trades. Use surgical veto tuning when the matching entry rule would be too broad.
- Do not spend more than 4 consecutive recommendations on upstream entry filters unless worst MAE or average MAE improves versus the previous run. If entry-filter experiments fail, return to surgical MAE/veto tuning.
- Use unmatched_bad_mae_clusters to identify genuinely new signature candidates. If a cluster is not covered by existing signature_hints, prefer recommending a dedicated surgical switch only when existing config keys cannot express it.
- Prefer surgical entry-veto signatures for one or two repeated deep-MAE patterns. Do not disable a surgical veto only because it removes a small winning PnL if it materially improves MAE, drawdown, or exposure quality.
- You can make a small, testable next move. 1 to 5 config changes is best.
- You can also make large changes. Feel free to use your quant expertise, and take deep insights from previous runs. The only thing I don't want is to use stop losses.

Hypothesis discipline:
Every recommendation becomes a testable hypothesis. Use hypothesis_result, hypothesis_family, and hypothesis_reason in experiment memory to avoid repeating failed ideas. Prefer new experiments that explain which metric should improve and why. If a prior hypothesis was rejected, do not retry the same family/threshold unless the new recommendation changes the mechanism, scope, or protected trade set.

Strategist discipline:
Use the Quant strategist plan as the research thesis. Prefer implementing exactly one next_experiments item when it can be expressed with legal config keys. If the strategist proposes a requires-code or new-profile idea that cannot be expressed in config, include it in strategy_hypotheses and choose a legal config-only experiment for changes[].

## Interpretation Notes
- This strategy exits with take-profit orders only, so a high win rate can hide capital being tied up for a long time.
- The best setting candidates are usually found by reducing slow-to-profit entries, not simply maximizing raw entry count.
- Focus first on buckets with low average PnL or long median hold time, then test stricter RSI/ADX/VWAP/VIX filters against those buckets.
